Abstract 
 
 
 
This thesis is about modeling a prototype of a polygeneration system based on solar 
power and reversible solid oxide fuel cell technology. 
 
The plant would consist basically in a Dish-Stirling collector field supported by a 
reversible solid oxide fuel cell unit. The idea behind the using of RSOFC is to distribute the solar 
energy along the day. This is very convenient for the power system so this kind of plant could 
have a great interest in the future. The operation and challenges of this plant are identified 
and analyzed. 
 
A great effort of this project has been spent in developing new necessary models for 
simulating the plant. The program used to simulate, DNA, has an extensive library but not a 
solid oxide electrolyzer cell, a parabolic trough solar collector nor a direct contact distillation 
membrane module (hollow fiber configuration). So a lot of literature has been compared in 
order to develop the named components.  
 
At the end, a complete interconnected model with all the elements combined in DNA 
was successfully performed. Then some results and interesting points were discussed. A simple 
case was performed under hypothetical conditions and the results indicated that with 200 
units (25kW) of Dish-stirling units, the system could be able to provide around 690 kW of 
constant power.

1. Introduction 
 
The Earth´s current situation is not very optimistic. There are well known facts such as 
ice melting and sea level rise that prove that the earth´s temperature is increasing. If this 
global warming continues, ecosystems will be greatly disturbed; weather conditions will 
become more extreme; less fresh water available… [1].  These are all indicators that humanity 
is overexploiting the Earth. In fact, the world population demand on nature is about 1.5 times 
what the biosphere can supply [2].  
The current world population is about 7 billion and, according to many studies, it is 
expected to increase up to 10 billion in the next 50 years [3].  Not only is that, but the lifestyle 
in developing countries is also changing towards a more consumptive behavior1. These facts 
will make the Earth´s situation more problematic and the solution a great challenge.  
Particularly, the extraction technologies for supplying the increasing demand on 
energy are a big responsible of this situation. The CO2 emission levels are to be reduced by 
limiting the primary energy consumption from fossil fuels and increasing the share of 
renewable sources in the world´s energy power mix. Among all the alternatives, wind, hydro 
and solar energy are meant to play an important role in the future [4]. 
 
Most of renewable energy sources derive from the solar radiation reaching the Earth 
which is about 120.000 TW [5]. Considering that the world´s energy demand is around 18 TW 
[4], there is plenty of energy free of CO2 ready to be used. However, one inconvenient of many 
of these sources is their natural intermittence or fluctuation because the power sources must 
achieve a certain degree of flexibility in order to maintain the reliability on the electricity 
supply. Another inconvenient is that renewable power technologies are not price competitive 
against the others (except hydro). These are two of the main barriers for the renewable power 
integration. 
 
In our power system, the plant that generates the cheapest energy will produce before 
than the others.  Thus, the cost efficiency [kWout/€] is more important than the energy 
efficiency2 [kWout/ kWin]. Currently, the RE plants are still more expensive (less cost effective) 
than the fossil fuel plants for example; nevertheless, the authorities apply some support 
mechanisms in order to make the RE more competitive and thus boost their integration in the 
electricity market. 
 
As said before, RE plants are not very flexible, i.e. they cannot choose when to 
produce. That is a very important characteristic because without flexibility it would be 
impossible to match the power produced to the power demand resulting in a very inefficient 
                                                          
1 Better quality of life in developed countries is associated to a greater consumption per capita. 
However, the consumption levels in some developed countries can be significantly reduced without 
compromising the quality of life. 
2 However, by improving the energy efficiency of one plant, the price per energy unit goes down 
==PAGE:13==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
12 
 
system. The solution for increasing their flexibility is to implement a storage system. There are 
many ways and forms of storing energy so each one will be used depending on the application: 
batteries, hydrogen production, flying wheels…  
 
This study is inspired in a solar plant design from R.K.Akikur [6]  in which solar energy is 
combined with a Reversible Solid Oxide Fuel Cell (RSOFC) complementing each other in order 
to produce constant power. In hours of peak radiation the RSOFC works as SOEC producing 
hydrogen, and else the RSOFC works as SOFC to generate power by using the produced fuel. 
The results for the study were quite optimistic indicating that it can generate 100kW of 
constant power at 0.068 $/kWh. 
 
In this work, a similar plant is designed but with a few modifications. The PV system 
will be substituted by a Dish-stirling system and a desalination plant will be included. The plant 
is meant to be a solution for a continuous and reliable power plant generation using just solar 
irradiation. On top of that, the large amount of heat usually wasted is used for sea water 
desalination. Potable water is a very valuable need and specially in locations where the solar 
irradiation is high; that is why this plant design could be a good solution. 
 
With this paper it is expected to evaluate the prototype plant from a design point of 
view and identify its weaknesses and strengths. In order to do that, the plant will be 
characterize as close to reality as possible by creating and using different models. Also the 
technical performance evaluation made in this report could be helpful for starting a feasibility 
analysis in which the economical part could be analyzed.  
The document begins with a small introduction to a few concepts that will be used 
later in the report. Then, a detailed explanation about the methodology used in this report 
including all the modeling.  Finally the main results are presented and discussed.

2.  Background 
2.1 DNA and EES 
 
 
The main software used in this study is the Dynamic Network Analysis (DNA). It is a 
software tool for simulation and analysis of energy systems. It contains models for the 
thermodynamic characteristics of several gas components, solid fuels and ashes, and water. 
Also, it has transport properties models for the different fluids. Furthermore, there is an open 
source library where different models for components are available such as burners, turbo-
machinery or heat exchangers, engines etc. The users are free to modify the library by adding 
or modifying components. 
 
In order to build the system, the different control volumes or components are 
connected by using nodes represented by integer numbers. Each component has some nodes 
and parameters assigned which will be used to solve the system; some external operation 
conditions might be needed as well. The system is solved when mass flow and thermodynamic 
state are defined at each node according to all the restrictions. DNA will automatically make a 
mass and energy balance in each control volume every time it is simulating. That is very 
important to have in mind when writing the rest of the equations in the source code in order 
to be mathematically consistent. DNA applies a modified Newton convergence method to 
solve the equation system that is why it is important to give a few start guesses of the final 
solution. Otherwise the method might not converge to any solution. 
 
Other very similar software used is the Engineering Equation Solver (EES). It is more 
flexible software than DNA where all the equations have to be written by the user with the 
possibility of using some predefined functions. Basically the user has to build the entirely 
equation system and EES will solve it. ESS also needs some guess values and limits in the 
variables in order to converge. It also has a useful library with thermodynamic and transport 
data for different fluids as refrigerants and brines.  
2.2 Concentrating solar collectors 
 
 
In solar thermal applications there is always an element that wants to be heated and 
for some applications like hot water domestic supply it is enough to absorb directly the sun 
irradiation. However, for other applications the sun energy needs to be supplied at higher 
temperatures. In order to do that it is necessary to reduce the heat losses and an easy way to 
do that is by decreasing the absorption area (absorber). But, since the energy delivered by the 
sun per area is constant, it is required to put an optical element between the sun ray´s and the 
absorber which will redirect the irradiation to the smaller area where the absorber is located. 
This element is called concentrator and the relation between the concentrator and the 
absorber areas is called concentration ratio which is an approximation of the number of times 
by which the irradiation flux on the absorber has increased. There is a wide range of 
==PAGE:15==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
14 
 
concentration ratios depending on the application but the biggest systems could reach values 
of 105. [7] 
 
The concentrator requires an accurate shape design and optical quality to get an 
efficient performance. There is an additional difficulty because they also need to be properly 
oriented towards the sun. To do that, they incorporate a tracking system which could control 
one or two axis depending on the configuration. These challenges become bigger when higher 
temperature levels are needed. In fact, there is a trade-off between increasing the area of the 
receiver to achieve better optical performance and decrease it to reduce the thermal losses. 
[7] 
 
This kind of systems always consists of a concentrator and a receiver, where the 
radiation is absorbed (absorber) and converted to some other energy form. There are different 
possible configurations [7]: 
 Concentrator 
o Reflection/Refraction 
o Focus line/point 
o Continuous/segmented 
 Receiver 
o Concave, flat or convex 
The energy that is actually reaching the receiver depends on the optical characteristics 
of the system and can be quantified by the following equation:  
               
1.1 
 
For the systems considered in this paper,   is the specular reflectance of the 
concentrator and    is the beam radiation3 (or direct radiation). It worth to say that only low 
temperature systems are able to collect the diffuse radiation as well so most of the 
concentrator systems only takes the direct radiation into account. The next three factors 
actually depend on the angle of incidence of radiation on the aperture, that is why the effect 
of the angle of incidence in these parameters is often combined in one single factor called the 
incidence angle modifier,     . The first factor,  , is the intercept factor which indicates how 
much of  the reflected radiation is actually reaching the absorber surface. The second,  , is the 
transmittance of any cover system on the receiver. And the third, , is the absorptance of the 
absorber defined as the radiation absorbed in relation to the radiation on its surface. In 
practice, the incidence angle modifier is calculated experimentally for each case resulting in a 
polynomial regression that estimates values for different incidence angle4 as can be seen in the 
example in Figure 1 [7].  
                                                          
3 Total or global radiation is composed of direct and diffuse radiation which is the portion reflected from 
the environment. 
4 Incidence angle refers to the angle between the normal of the aperture surface and the sun´s rays 
reaching the surface.

2.3 Two phase flow 
 
 
In thermal systems it is often that a fluid needs to be heated or cooled in a heat 
exchanger until the point that a phase change occurs inside the pipe. When that happens, the 
flow will experiment a transition where the temperature keeps constant (saturation point) 
while the fluid absorbs/releases heat. During this period, both phases coexist together and the 
transport mechanism is more complex than in a single phase flow. It is important to 
understand this because it will directly affect to the heat transfer performance of the 
component. In Figure 2 can be seen the evolution of the stream in an horizontal pipe when it is 
absorbing heat and how gradually changes from full liquid to full gas.  
 
Figure 2: Evolution of flow evaporating in a horizontal pipe 
 
 
The characteristics and properties of this transition flow have been studied and 
nowadays there are a considerable number of correlations available. Many of them are to be 
applied for very specific the external conditions so it is important to choose that one that fits 
your problem characteristics.

3. Polygeneration plant description 
The plant has been designed based on the co-generation system purposed by R.K. 
Akikur [6] where PTSC, photovoltaic panels and reversible solid oxide fuel cells are combined 
to produce constant power all day long just using the solar radiation. The plant case of this 
study works in the same way but three modifications have been made: 
1. The PV panels have been substitute for a Dish-stirling system. The reason behind doing 
this is that Dish-stirling systems are currently much more efficient and still potential to 
be economically competitive against other available technologies. Also, the plant in 
this study is bigger than the one presented in [6] and Dish-stirling systems suit better. 
2. Air is used to feed the RSOFC instead of oxygen. It doesn´t make a big difference but 
there is one small advantage: the air is directly available everywhere so any storage is 
needed. 
3. The waste heat is recycled for seawater distillation. Try to make the most of everything 
is the key to achieve efficient systems and here there is an opportunity of using more 
heat instead of wasting it to the ambient. On the other hand, it makes sense to use 
that heat for desalination since there is often a lack of fresh water at locations where 
solar resources are higher. 
In short, what the plant does is to deliver power to the grid by transforming the solar 
energy collected in the Dish-stirling system supported by the RSOFC in order to overcome the 
fluctuating nature of the solar radiation. The idea is that the Dish-stirling delivers part of its 
load to the RSOFC for producing fuel (hydrogen) during the peak hours of radiation (SOEC 
mode); and then during the low or zero radiation, the fuel produced is used to feed the RSOFC 
and thus still be able to cover the power demand (SOFC mode). At the same time, all available 
heat produced is used for sea water desalination. 
In order to successfully make the plant work, it is crucial to develop a management 
plan/schedule which takes into account the forecast solar radiation and energy demand and 
the fuel supplies. Done in the right way, the flexibility of the plant production would be greatly 
improved which has always been a weak point in many renewable energy sources.  
 
Before explaining in detail the plant operation, a description of the main components 
is featured below.  
 
3. 1 RSOFC 
 
 
A reversible solid oxide fuel cell is a device that is able to work either in fuel cell or 
electrolysis mode. In fuel cell mode, air and the fuel are supplied at high temperatures; then 
an electrochemical reaction takes place in the device resulting in power and heat production. 
On the other hand, in electrolysis mode, power is required to split a solution into the atoms it 
==PAGE:18==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
17 
 
is formed. The big units for power generation are made of multiple stacks connected in parallel 
and in each of them a number of cells are connected in series. 
 
Solid Oxide Fuel Cell technology has received interest in the past 20 years during which 
it has been greatly developed. It is currently implemented in co-generation plants designs with 
great results. However, there is a new perspective in this technology which has an especial 
interest with potential for improving the balancing of the power system. The reason is that 
RSOFC can produce power and heat (SOFC mode) using the fuel produced in SOEC mode 
meaning that they can be used as a storage system. [8] 
 
The key factor of a storage system is the roundtrip efficiency which evaluates how 
much energy can be delivered back to the system compared to the energy received. For large-
scale electrical energy storage, a competitive technology solution requires round-trip 
efficiencies near 80% plus operating durations of 1-8 h and power capacities from 1 kW to 10 
MW [9]. RSOFCs have potential to become an efficient solution but their round trip efficiencies 
are still low and expensive compared to others like batteries5.  Nevertheless, this technology is 
developing fast and currently round trip efficiencies higher than 70% can be achieved 
according to [10]. 
 
In this plant concerned, the RSOFC implemented uses pure hydrogen as a fuel (anode 
side) and air (cathode side) for the SOFC mode; and in SOEC mode, hydrogen is produced by 
electrolysis of water. The overall reactions taking place in each mode are presented down 
below. 
 SOFC 
Semi-reaction anode: 
                  
            
1.2.1

1.2.2

1.2.3 
 
 SOEC

1.3.1 
Semi-reaction cathode: 
                   
           
1.3.2 
Overall: 
   
            
        
    
1.3.3 
 
 
Now can be seen more clearly how the products (output) of one reaction are the fuel 
(input) for the other. Notice that in RSOFCs, both reactions take place at high temperatures 
around 500-1000°C.  
                                                          
5 However, the specific energy stored in a battery is too small for power systems applications. 
==PAGE:19==

18 
 
Furthermore, an exchange of electrons can be appreciated at the semi-reactions 
formulae (1.2.1, 1.2.2, 1.3.1 and 1.3.2) called for “Redox” reactions6. The number of electrons 
involved in these reactions together with the voltage in the cell will determine the electrical 
work delivered or supplied. In this case equals to:  
                                    
1.4 
Where   is faraday´s constant (charge for one mole of electrons) and   is the cell´s 
voltage. The result in 1.4 is dependent on moles of reactive utilized. 
Total energy variation of the reaction,    , is composed of the free or Gibbs energy 
variation,    , which evaluates the useful work available or reversible work, and the useless 
work associated with the entropy variation,     . The     determines whether a reaction is 
spontaneous or not; if       then it is spontaneous (SOFC case) and if       then 
external work needs to be applied (SOEC case). 
The Nernst potential is defined as the necessary voltage to get an electrical work equal 
to the free energy (Gibbs) variation in the reaction; also known as the reversible voltage. In the 
SOFC case, the Nernst potential minus the polarization losses (later explained) is the result that 
will define the electrical work produced. 
           
   
1.5 
 
On the other hand, the minimum electrical work that has to be applied in a SOEC is 
determined by the Nersnt potential plus the polarization losses. Nevertheless, that energy 
might not be enough to drive its unspontaneous reactions. The remaining energy can be 
applied from a heat source at higher temperature and/or directly increasing the power and 
thus the current flowing through the cells, which will produce more heat due to the Joule 
effect7. When no external heat is needed, it is called the thermo-neutral point and it occurs 
when the voltage equals to: [11] 
        
   
1.6 
 
                                                          
6 Redox reactions includes: oxidation reactions, which is the electrons loss, and reduction reactions, 
which is the gain of electrons.  
7 Despite the fact that increasing the current will imply a faster deterioration of the cells performance. 
==PAGE:20==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
19 
 
 
Figure 3: Schematic plot of voltage vs. current indicating the different operation modes of the RSOFC [11] 
As indicated before, the Nernst potential (Reversible voltage) gives the theoretical 
minimum (SOEC) or maximum (SOFC) electrical work but in reality part of the voltage is lost 
irreversibly due to polarization. There are three types of polarization: the ohmic, the activation 
and the concentration polarizations. The ohmic resistance stays constant while the other two 
vary depending on the current applied; i.e. ohmic polarization increases proportionally with 
the current while activation polarization and concentration polarization are dominant at low 
and at high current levels respectively. [11] 
 
Regarding the RSOFC unit installed in the plant, its stack temperature is the highest 
temperature in the system (besides the Dish-stirling systems), therefore an external heat 
source with higher temperature would be needed to transfer heat to the unit when running in 
SOEC mode. Instead, it is decided that the SOEC mode will run at its thermo-neutral point or 
over all time so the energy provided is just DC power. A control device will make sure to 
provide at least the necessary current at any time. The specifications for this unit are in Table 
1. 
Table 1: RSOFC specification (anode and cathode referred to fuel cell mode)

10 μm (Yttria Stabilized Zirconia)

3.2 STIRLING-DISH 
 
 
This unit is a combination of a parabolic dish concentrator, a cavity receiver and a 
Stirling motor coupled to an alternator. The concentrator consists of mirrors which reflect the 
sun ray´s into a smaller point called focus point. There it is the cavity receiver which absorbs 
that energy and uses it to warm the working gas in the Stirling engine. Inside the Stirling, the 
same mass of working gas (typically Helium or Hydrogen because of its high heat-transfer 
capabilities) is alternately heated and cooled, i.e. no fuel consumption. The motor works by 
expanding when the gas is hot and compressing when it´s cool and since less power is required 
to compress a cool gas than power is produced by expanding the hot gas, the motor delivers a 
positive net power production. Thereafter, this mechanical power is converted to electrical 
power by the alternator. [12] 
 
The Stirling cycle ideally consists of two isothermal and two isochoric processes (see 
Figure 4). From 1 to 2, an isothermal compression of the cold side takes place while it´s cooled. 
Then (2-3), the cool gas is pushed through the regenerator gaining some heat stored in the 
previous cycle (isochoric process). In process 3-4 the gas is expanded by heating and therefore 
transmitting mechanical power to the hot piston. Finally in process 4-1 (isochoric), the hot gas 
is pushed back again through the regenerator releasing heat which will be absorb by the 
regenerator for the next cycle. As can be appreciated, the regenerator is a very important 
component in the Stirling engine since it recuperates heat from the previous cycle instead of 
wasting it. 
 
Figure 4: Stirling states diagram and stages [12] 
==PAGE:22==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
21 
 
 
Stirling motors are meant to be the most efficient way to transform heat into 
mechanical mainly because they work at high temperatures and that´s an issue to take into 
account. Typical temperatures range from 650°C to 800°C or even more, resulting in 
efficiencies of around 30% to 40%. [12] 
Due to the fluctuating nature of the solar radiation, there are two control methods 
currently implemented for keeping the receiver temperature high: variable stroke and variable 
pressure. Variable pressure is most commonly used and it basically regulates the pressure by 
adding or removing gas inside the engine. The working gas pressures are in a range of 5 - 20 
MPa which, together with high temperatures, make the engine construction a challenge. [13] 
 
Regarding the parabolic dish concentrator, it has concentration ratios of around 500-
4000 which allow getting temperatures above 1000°C at the focus point. That is why Stirling 
and parabolic dish make a good match. Approximately, a system with a dish of 5.5 meters in 
diameter gives around 5 kWe and a 10 meters dish gives around 25 kWe (with 1000 W/m2 of 
solar irradiation). [12] 
 
One fact to consider is that the receiver of such systems in which the concentration 
ratio is high, the use of cover is sometimes not justified because any absorption of radiation 
would lead to an increase of its temperature. [7]  
All these systems have a two-axis tracking system installed to ensure the best 
performance. They virtually follow the sun´s path according to a mathematic logarithm which 
predicts the sun´s position at every time along the year. 
Stirling-Dish systems are quite compact units and easy to scale up, which makes it 
desirable for decentralize applications but also for big scale plants. It has the highest solar to 
electricity efficiency between the other solar technologies and it does not require much 
material so it is called to be an economical way to produce electricity. 
In this plant, between all the different models available, the McDonnell Douglas 25-
kWe System has been chosen because of its size and good references about its characteristics 
and performance (Table 2). 
==PAGE:23==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
22

3.3 PARABOLIC THROUGH SOLAR COLLECTOR 
  
 
PTSC consists of a parabolic cylindrical structure made of a material with high 
reflectance (collector) which will concentrate the solar irradiation into a smaller area situated 
at the focal line. At that line, there is a pipe (receiver) circulating the heat transfer fluid (HTF), 
which will absorb the irradiation resulting in an increase of its temperature along the pipe. 
PTSC is considered as a low to medium temperature solar thermal technology since the typical 
concentration ratios are around 10-100 and the outlet temperatures can be from 60-90°C for 
domestic applications up to around 400°C for power generation [15].  
 
The collector is usually equipped with a tracking control system to optimize the solar 
power captured. There are different tracking configuration systems but they are basically 
based on photo-sensors which will active small motors to ensure that the collector is 
continuously facing the sun. However, these tracking systems have their limitations ,i.e. 
maximum rotation angle or number of rotating axes, so the incidence angle of the solar beam 
radiation will not be always optimal especially in the mornings and in the evenings when the 
sun is low. [16] 
 
The receiver or pipe in this case, is usually made of steel and becomes really hot 
reaching higher temperatures than the fluid inside. For that reason, to avoid a lot of heat loss 
to the ambient, the receiver is covered with a glass tube leaving a space gap between them. In 
that space there could be a gas at low pressure or just a vacuum space. In such a way, the 
irradiation flux can still go through the glass due to its high transmittance and the heat losses 
are considerably reduced. In fact, PTSC systems can collect up to around 60-70% of the 
incidence solar radiation depending on the optical characteristics and design. [7] 
 
Figure 6: PTSC components illustration [6] 
 
==PAGE:25==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
24 
 
 
The HTF´s most commonly used in PTSC are thermal oil, inorganic salt mixtures, 
hydrocarbons and water among others. If other fluid than water is used, it is driven through a 
heat exchanger to produce superheated steam, then that steam is directed to a turbine in 
order to produce power. On the other hand, by using water, superheated steam can be 
directly generated resulting in a simpler configuration and more efficient, plus higher steam 
temperatures can be reached. [17]. 
 
The PTSC system designed in this case is a direct steam generator where liquid 
pressurized water is coming in and a phase change takes place inside the pipe to get 
superheated steam at the end of the pipe. Then the steam will be preheated again and finally 
used to feed the SOEC. The specifications are in Table 3.

3.4 DIRECT CONTACT DISTILLATION MEMBRANE 
 
 
There are several techniques currently implemented for seawater desalination such as 
low pressure boiling or reverse osmosis (RO). Among them, membrane distillation (MD) is 
becoming more and more an attractive solution as the technology develops. MD is a thermal 
separation process where only the water vapor (or other volatile) passes through a 
microporous hydrophobic membrane driven by the vapor pressures gradient originated by the 
temperature difference between both sides of the membrane [18]. The feed side is where the 
warm seawater flows and the other side is the permeate side where cold fresh water is 
==PAGE:26==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
25 
 
flowing; both sides have a constant flow. Then, due to this vapor pressure difference indicated 
before, water evaporates from the feed side, passes through the membrane and condensates 
on the permeate side yielding in a mass flow increase of fresh water. 
 
The cold and warm streams are in contact through the membrane therefore heat 
transfer occurs, leading to a decrease and increase of the outlet temperatures on the feed and 
permeate side respectively. The counter-flow configuration is preferred to keep low operating 
temperatures and that results in an almost constant temperature difference along the surface 
in contact (see Figure 7). Notice that the vapor pressures are related to liquid-vapor interfaces 
at the temperatures of the closest layer to the membrane (TFm and TPm) meaning that flow 
transport characteristics are playing an important role as well and not just the fluid 
temperature. 
 
Figure 7: Example of temperatures along the surface length in DCMD (temperatures correspond to Figure 8.b) 
 
 
Other important fact to consider is the membrane liquid entry pressure (LEP) which 
will set the limit for the applied transmembrane pressure defined as the hydrostatic pressure 
minus the vapor pressure (        and         ). Keeping that value below the limit will 
avoid the liquid from entering inside the pores. Notice that the hydrostatic pressure doesn´t 
affect to the permeate flux but on the other hand it is important to prevent the porous from 
flooding. 
Regarding the membrane characteristics, according to all the working demands above 
indicated, it should be with [19]: 
i. 
High degree of permeability with optimum porosity and pore size. 
ii. 
High hydrophobicity and small maximum pore size in order to get high LEP values. 
iii. 
Low thermal conductivity with high thickness and porosity. 
iv. 
Good mechanical and chemical resistance characteristics. 
20 
25

35 
40 
45 
50 
55 
60 
65

0 
0.2 
0.4 
0.6 
0.8 
1

==PAGE:27==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
26 
 
Unlike other techniques, MD process just needs a low grade heat source to operate 
such as solar, waste heat, etc. In fact, this process has potential advantages compared to other 
mechanisms [18]: 
i. 
It operates at lower temperatures and hydrostatic pressures. 
ii. 
Close to total rejection of non-volatile solute. 
iii. 
Salt concentration doesn´t affect that much to the performance. 
iv. 
It is not limited by high osmotic pressure or concentration polarization. 
Furthermore, the permeate flux or water distilled in this case can achieve easily over 
35 l/m2h and even up to 81.5 l/m2h with a feed inlet temperature of just 60°C compared to the 
18-34 l/m2h for commercial RO systems. Even though these are results at laboratory scale yet, 
they have a promising future. [20] 
 
Despite there are different configurations for DCMD, a hollow fiber unit is going to be 
used in this study. In Figure 8.a can be seen the design of this kind of units is a shell in tube and 
there it is indicated the position of the inlets and outlets for each flow. Inside the shell there 
are lots of fibers in which the Feed flows while the Permeate flows around them. A common 
parameter from these units is the packing density, which relates the cross area occupied by 
the total number of fibers against the available cross section area from the shell. 
 
Figure 8 :  Scheme of a) a hollow fibers module and b) the mass and heat transfer through the membrane [18] 
 
In the plant case of this study, several units are fed by seawater preheated using the 
waste heat from the plant operation. This waste heat comes mostly from the RSOFC; however 
there is also an opportunity to recycle the heat transferred to the permeate flow during the 
distillation process as suggested in [21].  At that article, Lin suggests to put an extra HX (SWP4 
==PAGE:28==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
27 
 
in Figure 9) which will transfer some heat from the outlet permeate stream to the seawater 
stream before it comes in to the main HX (SWP3 in Figure 9) where the main heat source is 
used; in this case, the main source is the waste heat from the RSOFC . This system has been 
implemented in the plant expecting a greater performance in terms of fresh water production 
and heat recycling. 
 
The distillation system of the plant will consist of a number of hollow fiber modules set 
in parallel and the seawater stream will be distributed equally between the number of units 
needed. All units have a range of operation and thus a limit for how much water they can 
process; so the number of units connected will depend on how much seawater is heated up at 
that moment8. The specifications are in Table 4.

3.5 System operation 
 
As indicated before, the plant has two modes of operation: SOEC and SOFC mode. The SOEC 
mode operation is explained first in detail and then the few changes compared to SOFC are 
indicated. 
 SOEC mode (Figure 9) 
 
Water from the tank (1) is pumped to the PTSC (2) where it is heated up 
generating steam at 350°C (3). 
 
Before sending the steam to the RSOFC, it flows through the cathode pre-
heater gaining more heat (4) from the RSOFC cathode outlet (5). In this way 
some of the heat produced in the RSOFC is recovered. 
 
Preheated steam (4) is used then to feed the RSOFC cathode and anode 
respectively.  According to the equations of the SOEC reactions, the cathode 
                                                          
8 It would be better to put a heat storage tank in between in order to reduce the number of hollow fiber 
units during the peak hours of heat production. However, in practical terms the seawater will be 
processed sooner or later so the result at the end of the day is more or less the same. 
==PAGE:29==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
28 
 
outlet will be composed of mostly H2 but also water due to incomplete 
reactions; and the anode outlet will be composed of oxygen. Both outlets are 
ejected at the stack temperature (750°C).  
 
The off-fuel (H2 +H2O) flow, after it is cooled down at the cathode pre-heater 
(8), it will be cooled down again in the SWP1 transferring the heat to the sea 
water flow9 (41-43). The thermodynamic state at the outlet (9) is designed to 
be close to the saturation point of water but not below.  Later in the 
separator, the water in the off-fuel mixture condenses enabling to collect the 
water and the H2 separately (11 and 12) at ambient temperature. Water is 
stored at ambient pressure while the H2 is stored at 2 bar (13) by using C2. 
 
On the other hand, the oxygen coming out from the anode side (7) will 
transfer its heat to sea water flow in the SWP3 (46-47) and then released to 
the atmosphere. 
 
The sea water flows preheated up to 80°C with the RSOFC outlets (43 and 47) 
are mixed together. The resulting flow (50) is used to feed the DCMD system 
and then the outlet is discharged to the ambient (51). On the permeate side of 
the DCMD, fresh water is coming in (53); and the outlet (54) is used in the 
SWP4 to preheat the sea water (45-46) before it enters to the SWP3. Finally, 
the fresh water out from SWP4 (55) is conduced back to the tank at ambient 
pressure. 
 
Pumps 2, 3 and 4 drive the distillation system taking into account the LEP 
limits. 
 
At the same time, Dish-stirling system is producing power (210) for supplying 
the RSOFC and the remaining energy is sent to the grid. Since the power 
generated in the Dish-stirling is AC and the RSOFC works with DC (211), a 
rectifier must be implemented in order to connect both components. 
The system is set in a way that the RSOFC in electrolyzer mode is working at the 
thermo-neutral point or little bit over by controlling the power supplied. That will be the 
minimum power required since there is no external heat source.  
Regarding the storage system, the reason why the H2 is stored at higher pressure and 
the water doesn´t is because the energy required for compressing a gas is much higher than 
the necessary for a liquid; thus to discharge the H2 flow to ambient pressure and then 
afterwards compress it again would be a waste of energy. However, in the case of the water, it 
is justified because the wasted energy is minimum compared to greater complexity of storing 
pressurized water. 
Also, it is important to have in mind that the flow entering the separator (9) has to be 
at a higher temperature than the condensing temperature of water. Then, the separator will 
release heat until both water and H2 are at ambient temperature and completely separated in 
two phases. In order to do that the temperature in 9 is the condensing temperature at the 
pressure in 2 determined by pump 1; in such way, gas state at 9 is assured. Consequently, the 
higher pressures in 2, the less heat will be recycled in SWP1. 
                                                          
9 Sea water is  assumed to be at 15°C and a salt concentration of 35g/kg. 
==PAGE:30==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
29 
 
 
Figure 9: Scheme of the plant in SOEC mode 
 
 
 SOFC mode (Figure 10) 
The system is quite similar to the SOEC mode but with a few changes and new 
arrangements: 
 
The HX called cathode pre-heater is now the anode pre-heater and instead of 
water, now it is fed with H2 (14).  
 
The air will be supplied to the SOFC by a blower (C1) which will provide just 
enough energy to the fluid to overcome the pressure drop until it comes out at 
(23). Just like in the other side of the RSOFC, the air will be preheated in a HX 
called cathode pre-heater before entering into the RSOFC. 
 
The reactions taking place follow now the equations (1.3) of the SOFC mode 
shown before. As a result, the anode outlet (5) will be composed of mostly 
water but also H2 due to incomplete reactions (used fuel); and the anode 
outlet (7) will be composed of air poor in oxygen (off-gas). Still, both outlets 
are ejected at the stack temperature (750°C). 
 
Now, the steam generated at PTSC (3) is used to feed the SWP1 instead and 
raise the sea water temperature (41-42). Afterwards, the heat from the used 
fuel flow coming out the AP (8) is now used in a new component SWP2 to 
finally heat that sea water flow (42) up to 80°C (43). 
==PAGE:31==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
30 
 
 
Both outlets from the hot side of SWP1 and SWP2 (9 and 10) are directed to 
the separator/condenser. 
 
The Dish-stirling system is still producing power but less than before due to 
less radiation. However, the RSOFC is now able to produce power (211) to 
compensate using the stored fuel. This time, an inverter is needed to connect 
the power from the RSOFC (DC) (211) to the grid (AC)(212).

4. METHODOLOGY 
 
 
In this section, the steps followed for designing the power plant are described.  
1. The first thing to do is to make the models with the equations that will govern the 
behavior of each component. In order to do that, different literature was consulted to 
get the fundamentals behind each technology. Then the necessary equations were 
identify and written down in a code for DNA. 
 
2. Second, the models are compared against the literature in order to validate their 
results. Unfortunately not always was easy to compare but it helped to get an idea of 
the range of the values.   
 
 
 
 
3. Then the different components are dimensioned/sized according to the needs of the 
plant. Also some key parameters for the correct operation are discussed. 
 
 
4. Finally the total power plant is tested under different solar radiations. Here the 
performance of the plant in terms of power and potable water produced is presented. 
 
4.1. MODELLING 
 
 
The model for the whole system has been built in DNA. In this way the plant can be 
simulated under different operation conditions and easily evaluate its performance mainly in 
terms of power production and sea water distilled. Some of the components were already 
available in the DNA library, others are built by combination of simpler models and the rest 
had to be built modifying the source code or even from scratch. To build the models, the EES 
has been used for checking results and for consulting the database10. Down below is described 
component by component how they are built and the equations that govern their behavior: 
 
4.1.1 RSOFC 
 
Due to the complexity of creating a single model in DNA of a RSOFC that could operate 
in both modes, the two different modes, SOEC and SOFC, are treated as two different 
components. 
                                                          
10 Properties of some component were imported to DNA by using correlations. 
==PAGE:33==

32

gases composition based on equilibrium; and the power produced by using a detailed 
electrochemical model calibrated using empirical data. The data were taken for gas 
temperatures between 650-800°C and thus only valid in that range.

4.1.1.2 SOEC 
 
  
Unfortunately, there isn´t any model for SOEC in the DNA library. However, the 
supervisor of this paper had one model made by a former student that could be useful. The 
model was very limited since it was done by correlating results from an experiment in order to 
build an I-V curve. At the beginning, time was spent in making a few corrections and 
modifications in order to make a more general model; i.e. enable to choose number of cells 
and stacks, change the area of the cell …etc. Despite these changes, the model still had some 
limitations; for example it misses the dependence on the mass flow concentrations for the 
polarization curve or the possibility to change the thickness and characteristics of the anode, 
cathode and electrolyte. With these limitations, the behavior of the cell is not very trustable 
plus there is no way to define the complementary model to the previous SOFC model because 
it is not possible to define the same cell characteristics. At the end it was decided to make a 
new model for the SOEC based on the equations shown in [6, 23, 25, 26]. 
 
The new model (“SOEC 4”) is not as complete as the SOFC since it is assumed only 
one inlet (cathode) and it has to be pure water/steam. The presence of other species than 
hydrogen, oxygen and water will lead to errors in the results. The input parameters for the 
new “SOEC4” model are: outlet gas temperature, relative pressure drops of both sides, 
cells per stack (     and number of stacks (    . As in the SOFC, there are other design 
constants like the cell characteristics and dimensions but these are defined inside the 
code. 
 
First of all, the outlet pressures are calculated exactly the same way as in the 
previous section (Eq.4.1.1).  Then, the cell voltage and the current density are calculated 
using the power input.

voltage is defined similarly to the SOFC but adding the polarization instead :

4.1.2 Dish-stirling 
 
 
This model had to be partially built because although the Stirling engine was already 
available in the DNA library, the solar collector model is missing. The Stirling DNA model was 
made by Bent Lorentzen and it is based on a pseudo-stirling cycle13. The collector system in 
charge of providing the heat to the engine was implemented in a new model based on the 
equations in Richard B. Diver [12].

ambient temperature (     , irradiation (  ), relative losses through the structure compared 
to convection (           ), and the number of units (       ).

4.1.3 PTSC 
 
 
The Steam Generator PTSC model was totally written from scratch based on the 
equations found in the literature [7, 28, 29, 17, 30, 31, 32]. In short, the model calculates the 
outlet steam state conditions from the water flow inlet and the external atmospheric 
conditions. The model includes heat and pressure losses calculations along the pipe.  
The input parameters are: the direct solar radiation (   , solar ray´s angle of incidence 
(aoi), wind velocity (   , ambient temperature       , sky temperature       , the number 
of rows (ROWS) and the length (L). Other dimension and optical characteristics of the unit such 
as pipe aperture    , receiver diameters, reflectivity, absorptance, etc. They can be changed 
inside the code but they are not an input parameter.

4.1.4 DCMD 
 
 
This model was built first in EES based on the equations shown in Kim [18] for the 
Hollow fiber unit. The modeling along the entire fiber is done by dividing it in smaller segments 
or volumes of control and applying the balance equations using the mean properties or states 
in each of them (temperature, density, pressure…). If the system is not discretised, the non-
linear behavior of the system would lead to big errors in the results.

Regarding the evolution of both side flows on the axial direction, the variation of mass

Where       and       are the mean mass flows,      and      are mean velocities, 
and     and     are the heat capacities of the feed and permeate flow respectively. Notice 
that the velocities also vary together with the mass flows according to the cross area 
dimensions of the unit. It is also worth to say that when all the control volumes are linked, the 
outlets of one segment will be the inlets for the next one and at the end will form a big system 
were the only necessary inputs will be inlet conditions of the feed stream at the 1st segment 
and the inlet conditions of the permeate stream at the last segment (because they are in 
counterflow). 
  The model in DNA is implemented differently because it was a more practical 
solution. So instead, it is based on polynomial correlations built from the results given by EES 
model depending on just 2 variables: the feed mass flow entering the system and its 
temperature. The range of operation in the model for the mass flow for one unit is between 
0.05-0.15 kg/s; however higher values can be applied and then the number of units needed 
will come out as a result. On the contrary, the range of operation for the feed temperature has 
limits and it is decided to set them from 70°C to 90°C. Regarding the permeate flow, it is 
programmed to remain at a constant in-flow of 0.1 kg/s and at 25°C at the inlet. 
Other fact to be aware of is that DNA has not a properties database for sea water so 
simple water is used as an approximation. The consequences of that are that the temperatures 
slightly differ from the real model. That is why the outlet temperatures are also defined by 
correlations. Nevertheless, since the DNA does automatically an energy balance, it will 
simulate a heat loss to the ambient that represents that difference in media properties. 
At the end, the result parameters from the EES imported into the DNA model are: 
outlet temperatures (Tout), pressure drops      and the maximum hydrostatic transmembrane 
pressure applied (MaxHTP) on both sides, and the permeated vapor through the membrane 
(J). These parameters are put into the model and related with the external conditions 
accordingly. In the case of the MaxTHP, it is a bit different because the model in EES it is 
assumed atmospheric pressure at the outlets and that is not always the case in the system. 
Thus, the MaxTHP is corrected by adding that difference: 
                 
 
               
4.5.16 
 
 
Where         
 
 is the value calculated in EES for atmospheric pressure at the outlets,

Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
49 
 
  is the permeate or feed side,        is the pressure out and      is the atmospheric pressure. 
That value is always checked in order to assure that it is lower than the LEP. 
 
Eventually, once the parameters are kept constant, this model needs one pressure 
level on the permeate side (inlet or outlet) and the inlet state conditions for the feed stream 
meaning pressure, temperature and mass flow. 
 
4.1.5 Other components 
4.1.5.1 Compressors 
 
 
The compressor was available in DNA´s database under the name “COMPRE_1” made 
by Bent Lorentzen. However, the compressor used is “COMPRE_10” which is practically the 
same but instead of mechanical power, the input is electric power.  It is used to increase the 
pressure of the inlet gas at the expense of consuming power. The input parameters are: the 
isentropic efficiency (      and the electro-mechanical efficiency (     .  
First, the outlet flow state        is calculated based on the isentropic efficiency and 
the inlet conditions:

of the compressed fluid if there wasn´t entropy variation in the process, and        is the 
expected specific enthalpy of the outlet gas.

compressor plus the electric losses in the motor is defined by the mechanical efficiency:

4.1.5.2Pumps 
 
 
The pump model was also available in DNA already called “LIQPUM_1”.  Similarly to 
the compressors, it increases the pressure of the fluid but in this case the fluid must be in 
liquid state and real. The energy source for this component is also electricity by which 
transfers mechanical energy to the liquid. The input parameter is the overall efficiency of the 
component. 
 
Then, knowing the inlet conditions and the outlet pressure, the power consumption is 
determined like:

Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
50

4.1.5.3 Mixer 
 
 
For modeling the mixer of two streams, a new code was written named “MIXER2”. It is 
a very simple model that takes both streams and approximates the outlet pressure as the 
weighted average of the inlets. The outlet mass flow is calculated automatically by DNA. One 
requirement is that both inlets have to be the same media. 
                   
       
      
4.8.1 
 
4.1.5.4 Separator/Condenser 
 
 
The separator model is built by combination of two models due to technical issues 
with the program. First there is a separator which will split the stream into its basic elements, 
in this case H2 and water. Then both streams are cooled down separately until the ambient 
temperature more or less; the heat is just released to the environment (heat sink). Notice that 
in SOFC mode, there is an additional water stream coming in the condenser which will be also 
cooled down to the same temperature as the other two. Then, the two water streams are 
mixed with mixer2 and sent to the water tank. 
 
The first source code used to model the separator is “SEPARA_1”. It needs to be told 
which element of the stream is going to be split (H2) and the effectiveness (0 nothing and 1 
means total separation). Then, the heat sinks are modeled with “HEATSNK0” for the H2 and a 
modified version called “HEATSNK10” for the water stream/s. The reason of using two 
different is that heatsnk0 doesn´t recognize when a phase change takes place. Heatsnk10 was 
includes a modification that allows to manually specified the outlet media, so now the 
problem can be solved by defining the outlet as liquid water (H2O-L).  
 
4.1.5.5 Rectifier/Inverter 
 
 
The AC/DC component necessary for the connection between de RSOFC and the Dish-
stirling system or the grid is modeled by combination of two simpler components. Actually it is 
the same component repeated which is a generator; its code name is “SIM_GENE”.  
 
In principle, the generator is meant to produce power from the mechanical power 
applied in its shaft. The relation between them is the input parameter      : 
==PAGE:52==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
51 
 
     
   
      
 
4.9.1 
 
 
The rectifier or inverter is basically an electronic device with an electric efficiency. By 
connecting one “electric motor” and a generator, an efficiency electricity-electricity can be 
achieved; that is the principle used. Then, one of them will have the power node as an input 
(electric motor)16 and the other as an output (generator) and their combined efficiency will be 
the AC/DC efficiency.   
                  
4.9.2 
 
  
4.1.5.6 HX´s 
 
 
There are two kinds of heat exchangers used in the model: one that the outlet 
temperature can be fixed, “HEATEX_1” and other where the effectiveness is the additional 
parameter, “HEATEX_4”. The first one is used for the heat exchangers for the distillation 
system and the other for the anode and cathode pre-heaters. The reason of having two 
different models is that “HEATEX_1” was more convenient for the design although 
“HEATEX_1” is a bit unrealistic component when simulating different operation conditions. On 
the contrary, the heatex_4 seems to model a real component better because the outlet 
temperatures vary under different conditions according to the effectiveness parameter.  
 
In the first model heatex_1, both mass flows and one outlet temperature have to be 
set and the other will be calculated by DNA making the energy balance. On the other hand, the 
heatex_4 uses the parameter input effectiveness to add one restriction, so now only two 
conditions have to be set; for example both mass flows are set and then the outlet 
temperatures will be calculated.  
               
                                
                
 
4.10.1 
               
                              
                
 
4.10.2 
 
 
 
Where the 1-2 is the hot stream and 3-4 is the cold stream and      is the specific heat. 
In the model, the effectiveness will be assumed to be 0.8. 
 
                                                          
16 When working as a electric motor, DNA sends a warning but that is because the power is not 
supposed to be an input. 
==PAGE:53==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
52 
 
 
4.2 Validation 
 
For validating the PTSC, first the heat losses from the outer surface of the receiver to 
the ambient are compared to the results in Figure 9 in [34] for “no-sun”. To do that, the 
dimensions and thermal characteristics of the receiver and absorber were changed 
accordingly. As seen in Figure 15, both results match perfectly. 
 
Figure 15: Validation of PTSC model. Heat losses. 
 
 
A second way to validate the model was to compare the power absorbed. The 
reference chosen was Akikur´s paper [6] despite the fact that some information about the 
dimensions and materials used in the receiver and cover were missing. That is the reason why 
both curves don´t match. Looking at the figure, it can be appreciated that they have the same 
tendency with slightly more difference for higher radiations. Since more heat is absorbed in 
the Model, it means that it is better insulated by a greater air/vacuum gap for example. That 
could also explain that a higher radiations, when the temperatures are higher, the Akikur´s 
model losses more energy.

Regarding the DCMD, the model is tested against the results in Li_Hua Cheng study

the model was compared to the model in Akikur´s paper using his equations for the ohmic 
and activation losses instead of the ones taken from the SOFC model. The results matched

proven wrong. 
 
4.3 Dimensioning 
 
 
In this section it is explained the way the different models are dimensioned in order to 
be coupled together. There are two main subsystems in the plant, the Dish-stirling collectors 
and the storage system. Both can be relatively easy to scale up by adding more collector units 
or solid oxide cell stacks. An interesting result of this plant would be to know how much power 
could continuously produce for the size of the system. Actually, the sizes of each subsystem 
are related depending on the solar radiation available during the day. For example: 
 
 
Figure 18: Solar radiation distribution. Case A and B 
 
Figure 18 represents two hypothetical cases were two different solar radiation 
distribution takes place. Both cases A and B receive the same amount of total energy but one 
of them has a high energy peak while the other is more uniform. If a constant power needs to 
be produced with this energy source by the plant purposed in this paper, the storage 
subsystem must be larger in case B than in case A. Another fact to take into account is the 
round-trip efficiency of the storage system. Since more power has to be stored in case B, it will 
be more affected by the round-trip efficiency and the possible power to deliver will be less.  
0 
5 
10 
15 
20 
Case A 
Case B 
==PAGE:56==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
55 
 
 
Once said that, the next step is to start dimensioning the components. Ideally the 
design would start by getting a profile of the solar radiation available and the demand to be 
covered and then size the system accordingly. In this paper, a considerable size for a RSOFC 
will be chosen first; then the rest of the components in the storage system will be dimensioned 
and afterwards will be evaluated under different radiations. The Dish Stirling field will be 
assumed big enough to cover the SOEC demand. 
 
To start with, it´s been decided that the RSOFC should be able to deliver around 500 
kW with a fuel utilization of 0.8 which is the power of around 20 units of the Dish-Stirling. This 
fact leads to a RSOFC of minimum around 150 stacks and 70 cells per stack with an H2 
consumption of 0.011 kg/s. Then, once the size of the RSOFC is known, the mass flow of steam 
coming into the SOEC must be determined for designing the PTSC. As mentioned before, since 
there is no other heat source at higher temperature than the outlet gases of the RSOFC, the 
SOEC has to be forced to operate over the thermo-neutral point. Ideally, the component could 
work on the thermo-neutral point because is where the efficiency is higher. If the SOEC is 
running way over that point, the power will be wasted and higher degradation in the cell will 
occur. The thermo-neutral state is achieved at a cell voltage of 1.285 V however the practical 
voltage in this plant will be a bit higher in order to generate the extra heat for heating up the 
steam inlet flow. Now is all about finding that curve of minimum power necessary like it has 
been done in Table 5. It is recommendable to start looking for the state where the SOEC 
produces the same H2 rate as it is consumed in the SOFC at the rated power. Then define a 
range of possible operation points around that because afterwards the PTSC has to be 
designed accordingly.  
 
In the PTSC design, it is decided to keep the outlet temperature at 350°C. Then, the 
mass flowing through the pipe will be set by the direct solar radiation on the collector. Now 
depending on the climate characteristics of the location, a decision should be made about the 
desired rated H2 production and match it with the usual high radiation. In this case it is chosen 
that the PTSC should deliver 0.16 kg/s at 350°C and 1.4 bar under a solar radiation of 
800W/m2. As a result, the H2 produced in the SOEC is slightly higher than the necessary in the 
SOFC for the rated power. In such a way it is expected a higher degree of security in supplies. 
The PTSC system will then consist of 2 parallel rows of 160 meters and 2.5 meters of aperture. 
 
Other issue to take into account in the system design is the pressure drops. Pump 1 is 
in charge of driving the steam side and the pressure that needs to be applied must be 
sufficient to flow all the way until the condenser. This pressure applied by pump 1 is not 
optimal if it is too high neither. The reason behind is that the higher pressure, the higher 
temperature of condensation so less heat is available to be extracted before it goes into the 
condenser (point 9). On the other hand, there is another critical point in terms of pressure in 
the distillation system. The pump 3 has to give enough pressure to overcome the losses in the 
component DCMD and SWP4 to reach the tank again; but in the same time the pressure is 
limited by the LEP in the DCMD. So the possibility to recover the heat at the outlet of the 
permeate side is conditioned by the pressure drop in the heat exchanger. 
 
Regarding the number of units needed in the distillation system, it has already been 
said that the criteria is to use as minimum units as possible but in the model the numbers of 
==PAGE:57==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
56 
 
minimum units is varying according to the inlet flow in that moment. It would be more optimal 
to store that water in an insulated tank and use it in a continuous flow. Nevertheless, the 
model is useful to have a fair approximation. 
 
After this, all components are now dimensioned and connected properly so in the next 
section the results will be presented. 
  
 
 
==PAGE:58==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
57 
 
 
5. Results and Discussion 
 
In this section the performance results of the main components modeled is shown and 
analyzed as well as the operation of the entire plant. The simulations are done in steady state 
operation and then the results are interpolated. The outlet conditions were assumed 30°C of 
air temperature, 30°C of sky temperature and 5m/s wind speed. 
Starting with the SOEC, the next figure presents the concentration polarization curve 
made for the electrolyzer (750°C) depending on the molar fraction of the species at the outlet. 
It can be seen that the maximum current that system can handle varies a lot with the H2 
concentration. This is the main reason why is not possible to have high fuel utilizations with 
high powers or H2 production rates. 
 
 
Figure 19: Concentration polarization curve 
The Table 5 shows the necessary voltage to enter in the exothermic voltage related 
with the inlet flow. Other interesting parameters are shown as well. These values were used in 
order to design the PTSC and it can be appreciated that at 0.12 kg/s is when it produces the 
amount of hydrogen necessary to produce around 500 kW in SOFC mode (Table 7). These 
values give an idea of the round trip electrical efficiency of the system:

the pump 1 and the condensation temperature. One inconvenient is that at lower pressures, 
the steam is more present in the PTSC pipe length and that results in higher pressure drops.

that is not consumed is just wasted at the outlet. At this point it is well known by the reader

not clear if the UF can be changed freely.

Nevertheless, there is a small inconvenient and it is that the inlet mass flow will

to remove from the SOFC (the fuel is carrying it). So at the end, it seems like a more detailed 
analysis of the whole plant is necessary and it should be able to tell what is best.

First of all, it can be seen that the potable water production is much higher in the SOFC 
mode since a lot of heat is released during the hydrogen oxidation. Assuming that the SOEC 
mode is working 10 hours per day when the radiation is high (average 600 W/m2) and that the 
SOFC is working 14 hours at an average of 0.007 kg/s of H2; the plant could distillate around 
5300 liters per day enough for at least 500 people. 
 
Regarding the efficiencies, the SOFC operates in an average of 45% of electric 
efficiency and the SOEC of around 94%. This big difference is because in the SOFC a lot of heat 
is involved in the reaction while in the SOEC only a small part of the power is lost by the 
irreversibilities. By combining both efficiencies, the round trip efficiency of the system is 
defined, around 42%. Then, the demand during the lack sun is much more expensive to 
deliver. Only about 42% of the extra power produced can be distributed among the hours with 
a lack of radiation. 
 
Regarding the Dish-stirling units, using the data in table 6 it can be seen that it is 
necessary around 100 units of 25kW to feed the SOEC of 70x150 cells. The minimum number 
of units depends on the level of irradiation at which the RSOFC changes to electrolyzer mode. 
For example, at less radiation higher number of Dish-stirling units is needed. An important 
design parameter will be to choose the radiation level at which the RSOFC changes to 
electrolyzer mode and that will be imposed by the demand and the variation of radiation along 
the day. 
 
Just in order to get an idea of the performance of the plant with numbers, a simple 
case is presented with rough calculations. Only the electric power generation will be 
considered and assuming a constant round-trip efficiency. Two cases will be compared with 
different solar radiation profiles in a scenario where a constant demand has to be supplied. 
==PAGE:63==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells

In Table 9 the results for four different conditions are shown. In order to make a fair 
comparison, the profile 1 and 2 gives the same total amount of radiation at the end of the day. 
It can be appreciated that a constant demand of around 700 kW could be covered with 200 
units of Dish-stirling systems; and that demand could rise up to 1044 kW with 300 units. Case 2 
and case 3 show the effect of the round trip efficiency change and the consequences of 
different solar radiation distribution along the day, respectively. Both cases had slightly 
difference in the maximum demand covered but less than expected. The reason could be that 
the difference between the cases wasn´t large enough.

6. Conclusions 
A complete model for the plant purposed at the beginning was successfully done. All 
the modeling work ended up to be much more complicated and time consuming than it could 
be expected. A deep research among many papers has been done in order to find the 
equations that govern each component and then interconnected. The whole process of 
understanding the technologies reading the papers and then writing the codes in DNA has 
been the real challenge of this work.  
The performance of each model has been validated against other models and 
experimental data. The only model that could not be completely compared to literature is the 
SOEC but it was only a specific part of it.  
After designing the plant and seen some of the results, it seems like this plant design 
has potential to become a good alternative for power generation. The total round trip 
efficiency is not very high yet but there are studies talking about efficiencies of 70%. It was 
estimated that under the hypothetical conditions presented in the example, a total power of 
690 kW could be constant supplied by using 200 Dish-stirling units (25kW) and a RSOFC unit of 
150x70 cells. 
Then, some interesting points have been discussed like the possibility to decrease the 
UF to get more power instead of heat and then increase the round trip efficiency for example. 
Also, in the example case, the results indicated that the variation of the UF didn´t have a big 
effect. However, the cases presented were maybe too similar in order to appreciate the 
magnitude of the influence of each parameter. Under more extreme situation like limiting the 
sun radiation to only 5 hours a day, the storage subsystem would play a bigger role. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:65==
Design of polygeneration system based on solar power and solid oxide cells 
 
 
64 
 
 
 
7. Recommendations for further 
work 
The complete study of the plant is a laborious job. In this paper only the first part of 
the analysis has been done.  To continue with this study it would be a good idea to do a 
thermo-economic analysis to detect possible improvements in design and then include the 
economical perspective to the analysis.  
Also, it could be interesting to modify the design like for example using the heat for a 
cooling plant or add a high pressure water storage tank to improve the supply of steam into 
the RSOFC. In addition, the possibility of recovering some heat in the condenser would be an 
important improvement because quite a lot of heat is wasted in there. 
Other interesting branch of study could be to place the plant in a specific area and run 
the model in DNA for a whole year against a weather database by Matlab. In this way the 
balance of hydrogen consumed and produced could be studied properly and then get the 
power produced and the water distilled. An optimal relation between the number of Dish-
Stirling units and the size of the RSOFC for that location could be found as well.

C ----------- COMPRESSOR H2 --------------- 
c Note that this component is here to assure a minimum pressure in 
the 
c tank. It can happen that the inlet has a higher pressure than the 
c specified outlet. In that case DNA will show an error but the 
only 
c consequence is that the power generated shouldn´t be taken into 
account 
STRUC COMP2 COMPRE_10 12 13 206 306 0.7 0.95 
ADDCO P 13 2

C RECTIFIER 
C It is modelled using two generators.RECTIF 1 transform el power 
to 
c mechanical with 100% eff and the RECTIF2 is a generator as well 
but 
c with the corresponding efficiency of the rectifier in question.

because 
c the power should not be an input in principle for this component

APPENDIX B. SOURCE CODES FOR THE MAIN COMPONENTS
